Architecture\\n\\n## Overview\\n\\nKubernetes integrates CNI plugins through the Container Runtime Interface (CRI), which abstracts container runtime details. The kubelet communicates with the container runtime (e.g., containerd) via gRPC, and the runtime is responsible for invoking CNI plugins during pod sandbox creation and teardown.\\n\\n## Key Components and Files\\n\\n### 1. CNI Plugin Invocation Flow\\n\\nThe primary CNI invocation happens through the following call chain:\\n\\n**`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go)**\\n- Orchestrates the overall pod creation process\\n- Manages the runtime service instance\\n- Coordinates both pod sandbox creation and container lifecycle\\n\\n→ **`createPodSandbox()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go)**\\n- Entry point for pod sandbox creation\\n- Calls `m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` with the sandbox configuration\\n\\n→ **`generatePodSandboxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go)**\\n- Generates the complete PodSandboxConfig from the v1.Pod specification\\n- Includes DNS configuration, hostname, port mappings, and networking setup\\n- Delegates to platform-specific config generators\\n\\n→ **`generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go, kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go)**\\n- Creates the LinuxPodSandboxConfig with network namespace setup\\n- Configures SecurityContext with NamespaceOptions\\n- Sets up Linux-specific networking features\\n\\n→ **`RunPodSandbox()` gRPC call (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go)**\\n- Sends RunPodSandboxRequest to the container runtime via gRPC\\n- The container runtime (e.g., containerd) receives this request\\n- The runtime then invokes CNI plugins with the network configuration\\n- Returns podSandboxId and network status (with IP addresses)\\n\\n### 2. Network Namespace Setup\\n\\n**`NetworkNamespaceForPod()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go)**\\n- Determines whether a pod should use the host network namespace or a pod-specific namespace\\n- Checks `pod.Spec.HostNetwork` flag\\n- Returns `runtimeapi.NamespaceMode_NODE` for host networking or `runtimeapi.NamespaceMode_POD` for pod networking\\n\\n**`NamespacesForPod()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go)**\\n- Comprehensive function that sets up all namespace options for a pod\\n- Handles network, IPC, and PID namespaces\\n- Integrates with RuntimeHandler for specialized runtime configurations\\n- Returns runtimeapi.NamespaceOption structure passed to the runtime\\n\\n**`generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go)**\\n- Implements Linux-specific namespace setup\\n- Calls `NamespacesForPod()` to configure network namespace\\n- Sets up SecurityContext with proper namespace options\\n\\n### 3. IP Address Management (IPAM)\\n\\n**`updatePodCIDR()` (pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go)**\\n- Updates the pod CIDR (Classless Inter-Domain Routing) configuration\\n- Called when the cluster networking configuration changes\\n- Communicates the cluster's pod CIDR to the runtime via `kl.getRuntime().UpdatePodCIDR(ctx, cidr)`\\n- The container runtime then propagates this information to CNI plugins\\n\\n**Pod IP Allocation in PodSandboxConfig:**\\n- The actual IP address allocation happens after RunPodSandbox returns\\n- The response includes `PodSandboxNetworkStatus` containing the allocated IP address\\n- Retrieved in `getPodSandboxStatus()` where the network status (including IP) is extracted\\n- The IP is taken from `podSandbox.Network.Ip` field\\n\\n**IPAM Integration Points:**\\n- CNI IPAM plugins are invoked by the container runtime\\n- kubelet passes necessary network configuration through PodSandboxConfig\\n- The Kubernetes controller manager (not kubelet) manages the overall IP address allocation and assignment to nodes\\n- kubelet simply reports the allocated IPs back to the API server\\n\\n### 4. Network Plugin Manager (Coordinator)\\n\\n**`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go)**\\n- Central orchestrator for all pod lifecycle operations\\n- Manages the `RuntimeService` instance (gRPC client to container runtime)\\n- Coordinates:\\n  - Pod sandbox creation and teardown\\n  - Container creation and startup\\n  - Network setup and teardown\\n  - Integration with device managers and security contexts\\n\\n**`RuntimeService` Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go)**\\n- Defines the interface that the kubelet uses to interact with container runtimes\\n- Core method: `RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, config *PodSandboxConfig, runtimeHandler string) (string, error)`\\n- Also provides: `StopPodSandbox()`, `RemovePodSandbox()`, `PodSandboxStatus()`, etc.\\n\\n**`remoteRuntimeService` (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go)**\\n- gRPC client implementation of RuntimeService\\n- `RunPodSandbox()` method creates a gRPC request and sends it to the container runtime\\n- Handles connection management and error handling\\n- The actual CNI invocation happens on the runtime side (e.g., containerd's CNI integration)\\n\\n**`instrumented_services.go` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/instrumented_services.go)**\\n- Wraps the RuntimeService to add:\\n  - Metrics collection\\n  - Performance monitoring\\n  - Tracing and observability\\n\\n### 5. Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**DNS Configuration (pkg/kubelet/network/dns/)**\\n- `dns.go`, `dns_other.go`, `dns_windows.go`\\n- Configures DNS settings for pods\\n- Works in conjunction with CNI to provide complete networking setup\\n\\n**Network-related Kubelet Methods (pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go)**\\n- `providerRequiresNetworkingConfiguration()`: Determines cloud provider network requirements\\n- `updatePodCIDR()`: Handles cluster CIDR updates\\n- `GetPodDNS()`: Provides DNS configuration to containers\\n\\n**Container Interface (pkg/kubelet/container/)**\\n- `RuntimeHelper` interface: Defines methods kubelet uses to get pod-specific information\\n- `sync_result.go`: Tracks `SetupNetwork` and `TeardownNetwork` sync actions\\n\\n**CRI API Definitions (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/)**\\n- `services.go`: RuntimeService interface definition\\n- `api.proto`: Protocol buffer definitions for:\\n  - `PodSandboxConfig`: Complete pod configuration including networking\\n  - `LinuxPodSandboxConfig`: Linux-specific configuration with namespace options\\n  - `NamespaceOption`: Network namespace specification\\n  - `PodSandboxNetworkStatus`: Response containing allocated IP addresses\\n  - `RunPodSandboxRequest` and `RunPodSandboxResponse`: gRPC message definitions\\n\\n## CNI Integration Summary\\n\\nThe CNI integration in Kubernetes works as follows:\\n\\n1. **Pod Creation Request**: When a pod needs to be scheduled, kubelet receives the pod specification\\n\\n2. **Network Configuration**: kubelet generates a PodSandboxConfig that includes:\\n   - Network namespace mode (pod or host)\\n   - Port mappings\\n   - Hostname and domain\\n   - DNS configuration\\n   - Pod CIDR information\\n\\n3. **CRI Call**: The kubelet calls the container runtime's RunPodSandbox method via gRPC with the config\\n\\n4. **CNI Plugin Invocation** (on runtime side): The container runtime invokes CNI plugins:\\n   - Network plugin: Sets up network interfaces and bridge\\n   - IPAM plugin: Allocates IP addresses from the configured IP pools\\n   - Other plugins: Additional networking features (e.g., network policies)\\n\\n5. **Network Status Return**: The runtime returns the pod sandbox ID and network status (including allocated IP)\\n\\n6. **Pod Launch**: kubelet proceeds with container creation within the configured network environment\\n\\n7. **Network Teardown**: When the pod terminates, kubelet calls StopPodSandbox, and the runtime invokes CNI plugin cleanup (DEL action)\\n\\n## Key Design Principles\\n\\n- **Runtime Abstraction**: CNI invocation is entirely managed by the container runtime, not by kubelet directly\\n- **gRPC Communication**: All runtime interactions use CRI, a gRPC-based interface\\n- **Configuration-Driven**: Network setup is driven by the PodSandboxConfig structure\\n- **Platform-Specific**: Network setup varies per platform (Linux vs Windows)\\n- **Stateless**: kubelet reports network status but doesn't directly manage network state\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":318,"cache_read_input_tokens":53758,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":318},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a9d67e51-8744-4c47-9e9a-c422024e9ee9","uuid":"46eabd56-599f-4a45-9710-3ed2e03b46ac"}

Architecture\\n\\n## Overview\\n\\nKubernetes integrates CNI plugins through the Container Runtime Interface (CRI), which abstracts container runtime details. The kubelet communicates with the container runtime (e.g., containerd) via gRPC, and the runtime is responsible for invoking CNI plugins during pod sandbox creation and teardown.\\n\\n## Key Components and Files\\n\\n### 1. CNI Plugin Invocation Flow\\n\\nThe primary CNI invocation happens through the following call chain:\\n\\n**`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go)**\\n- Orchestrates the overall pod creation process\\n- Manages the runtime service instance\\n- Coordinates both pod sandbox creation and container lifecycle\\n\\n→ **`createPodSandbox()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go)**\\n- Entry point for pod sandbox creation\\n- Calls `m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` with the sandbox configuration\\n\\n→ **`generatePodSandboxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go)**\\n- Generates the complete PodSandboxConfig from the v1.Pod specification\\n- Includes DNS configuration, hostname, port mappings, and networking setup\\n- Delegates to platform-specific config generators\\n\\n→ **`generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go, kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go)**\\n- Creates the LinuxPodSandboxConfig with network namespace setup\\n- Configures SecurityContext with NamespaceOptions\\n- Sets up Linux-specific networking features\\n\\n→ **`RunPodSandbox()` gRPC call (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go)**\\n- Sends RunPodSandboxRequest to the container runtime via gRPC\\n- The container runtime (e.g., containerd) receives this request\\n- The runtime then invokes CNI plugins with the network configuration\\n- Returns podSandboxId and network status (with IP addresses)\\n\\n### 2. Network Namespace Setup\\n\\n**`NetworkNamespaceForPod()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go)**\\n- Determines whether a pod should use the host network namespace or a pod-specific namespace\\n- Checks `pod.Spec.HostNetwork` flag\\n- Returns `runtimeapi.NamespaceMode_NODE` for host networking or `runtimeapi.NamespaceMode_POD` for pod networking\\n\\n**`NamespacesForPod()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go)**\\n- Comprehensive function that sets up all namespace options for a pod\\n- Handles network, IPC, and PID namespaces\\n- Integrates with RuntimeHandler for specialized runtime configurations\\n- Returns runtimeapi.NamespaceOption structure passed to the runtime\\n\\n**`generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go)**\\n- Implements Linux-specific namespace setup\\n- Calls `NamespacesForPod()` to configure network namespace\\n- Sets up SecurityContext with proper namespace options\\n\\n### 3. IP Address Management (IPAM)\\n\\n**`updatePodCIDR()` (pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go)**\\n- Updates the pod CIDR (Classless Inter-Domain Routing) configuration\\n- Called when the cluster networking configuration changes\\n- Communicates the cluster's pod CIDR to the runtime via `kl.getRuntime().UpdatePodCIDR(ctx, cidr)`\\n- The container runtime then propagates this information to CNI plugins\\n\\n**Pod IP Allocation in PodSandboxConfig:**\\n- The actual IP address allocation happens after RunPodSandbox returns\\n- The response includes `PodSandboxNetworkStatus` containing the allocated IP address\\n- Retrieved in `getPodSandboxStatus()` where the network status (including IP) is extracted\\n- The IP is taken from `podSandbox.Network.Ip` field\\n\\n**IPAM Integration Points:**\\n- CNI IPAM plugins are invoked by the container runtime\\n- kubelet passes necessary network configuration through PodSandboxConfig\\n- The Kubernetes controller manager (not kubelet) manages the overall IP address allocation and assignment to nodes\\n- kubelet simply reports the allocated IPs back to the API server\\n\\n### 4. Network Plugin Manager (Coordinator)\\n\\n**`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go)**\\n- Central orchestrator for all pod lifecycle operations\\n- Manages the `RuntimeService` instance (gRPC client to container runtime)\\n- Coordinates:\\n  - Pod sandbox creation and teardown\\n  - Container creation and startup\\n  - Network setup and teardown\\n  - Integration with device managers and security contexts\\n\\n**`RuntimeService` Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go)**\\n- Defines the interface that the kubelet uses to interact with container runtimes\\n- Core method: `RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, config *PodSandboxConfig, runtimeHandler string) (string, error)`\\n- Also provides: `StopPodSandbox()`, `RemovePodSandbox()`, `PodSandboxStatus()`, etc.\\n\\n**`remoteRuntimeService` (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go)**\\n- gRPC client implementation of RuntimeService\\n- `RunPodSandbox()` method creates a gRPC request and sends it to the container runtime\\n- Handles connection management and error handling\\n- The actual CNI invocation happens on the runtime side (e.g., containerd's CNI integration)\\n\\n**`instrumented_services.go` (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/instrumented_services.go)**\\n- Wraps the RuntimeService to add:\\n  - Metrics collection\\n  - Performance monitoring\\n  - Tracing and observability\\n\\n### 5. Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**DNS Configuration (pkg/kubelet/network/dns/)**\\n- `dns.go`, `dns_other.go`, `dns_windows.go`\\n- Configures DNS settings for pods\\n- Works in conjunction with CNI to provide complete networking setup\\n\\n**Network-related Kubelet Methods (pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go)**\\n- `providerRequiresNetworkingConfiguration()`: Determines cloud provider network requirements\\n- `updatePodCIDR()`: Handles cluster CIDR updates\\n- `GetPodDNS()`: Provides DNS configuration to containers\\n\\n**Container Interface (pkg/kubelet/container/)**\\n- `RuntimeHelper` interface: Defines methods kubelet uses to get pod-specific information\\n- `sync_result.go`: Tracks `SetupNetwork` and `TeardownNetwork` sync actions\\n\\n**CRI API Definitions (staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/)**\\n- `services.go`: RuntimeService interface definition\\n- `api.proto`: Protocol buffer definitions for:\\n  - `PodSandboxConfig`: Complete pod configuration including networking\\n  - `LinuxPodSandboxConfig`: Linux-specific configuration with namespace options\\n  - `NamespaceOption`: Network namespace specification\\n  - `PodSandboxNetworkStatus`: Response containing allocated IP addresses\\n  - `RunPodSandboxRequest` and `RunPodSandboxResponse`: gRPC message definitions\\n\\n## CNI Integration Summary\\n\\nThe CNI integration in Kubernetes works as follows:\\n\\n1. **Pod Creation Request**: When a pod needs to be scheduled, kubelet receives the pod specification\\n\\n2. **Network Configuration**: kubelet generates a PodSandboxConfig that includes:\\n   - Network namespace mode (pod or host)\\n   - Port mappings\\n   - Hostname and domain\\n   - DNS configuration\\n   - Pod CIDR information\\n\\n3. **CRI Call**: The kubelet calls the container runtime's RunPodSandbox method via gRPC with the config\\n\\n4. **CNI Plugin Invocation** (on runtime side): The container runtime invokes CNI plugins:\\n   -
